<th scope="row">Waterways</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Creek_(Indiana)" title="Pigeon Creek (Indiana)">Pigeon Creek</a></td>

<th scope="row">Airports</th>

</tr>
<tr class="mergedtoprow">
<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://www.evansvillegov.org" rel="nofollow">City of Evansville</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Evansville</b> is a city in and the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vanderburgh_County,_Indiana" title="Vanderburgh County, Indiana">Vanderburgh County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-5">[5]</a></sup> The population was 117,429 at the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>. As the state's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Indiana" title="List of cities in Indiana">third-largest city</a> and the largest city in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Indiana" title="Southern Indiana">Southern Indiana</a>, it is the commercial, medical, and cultural hub of <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Indiana" title="Southwestern Indiana">Southwestern Indiana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Illinois-Indiana-Kentucky_tri-state_area" title="Illinois-Indiana-Kentucky tri-state area">Illinois-Indiana-Kentucky tri-state area</a>, home to over 911,000 people. The <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">38th parallel</a> crosses the north side of the city and is marked on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_69_in_Indiana" title="Interstate 69 in Indiana">Interstate 69</a>.</p>
<p>Situated on an <a href="/wiki/Meander" title="Meander">oxbow</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>, the city is often referred to as the "Crescent Valley" or "River City". As testament to the Ohio's grandeur, early French explorers named it La Belle Riviere ("The Beautiful River"). The area has been inhabited by various cultures for millennia, dating back at least 10,000 years. <a href="/wiki/Angel_Mounds" title="Angel Mounds">Angel Mounds</a> was a permanent settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> from 1000 AD to around 1400 AD. The city itself was founded in 1812.</p>
<p>The broad economic base of the region has helped build an economy which is known for its stability, diversity, and vitality. Four <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a> companies (<a href="/wiki/Accuride_Corporation" title="Accuride Corporation">Accuride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berry_Plastics" title="Berry Plastics">Berry Plastics</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springleaf" title="Springleaf">Springleaf</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vectren" title="Vectren">Vectren</a>) are headquartered in Evansville, along with the global operations center for NYSE company <a href="/wiki/Mead_Johnson" title="Mead Johnson">Mead Johnson</a>. Three other companies traded on the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> (Escalade, <a href="/wiki/Old_National_Bank" title="Old National Bank">Old National Bank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shoe_Carnival" title="Shoe Carnival">Shoe Carnival</a>) are also headquartered in Evansville. The city is home to public and private enterprise in many areas, as Evansville serves as the economic hub of the region.</p>
<p>A popular tourist destination for the region, Evansville is home to <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Evansville" title="Tropicana Evansville">Tropicana Evansville</a>, the state's first casino, <a href="/wiki/Mesker_Park_Zoo_and_Botanic_Garden" title="Mesker Park Zoo and Botanic Garden">Mesker Park Zoo and Botanic Garden</a>, one of the oldest and largest zoos in the state, and a robust <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Evansville,_Indiana" title="Sports in Evansville, Indiana">sports tourism industry</a>. The city has several well known educational institutions. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">University of Evansville</a> is a small private school located on the city's east side, while the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Indiana" title="University of Southern Indiana">University of Southern Indiana</a> is a larger public institution located just outside the city's westside limits. Other local educational institutions have also garnered praise and attention, including nationally ranked <a href="/wiki/Signature_School" title="Signature School">Signature School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_Public_Library" title="Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library">Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library</a>. In 2008, Evansville was voted the best city in the country in which "to live, work, and play" by the readers of <a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a>, and in 2009 the 11th best.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><i>See main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Evansville,_Indiana" title="History of Evansville, Indiana">History of Evansville, Indiana</a></i>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>There was a continuous human presence in the area that became Evansville from at least 8,000 BC by <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indians</a>. Archaeologists have identified several archaic and ancient sites in and near Evansville, with the most complex at <a href="/wiki/Angel_Mounds" title="Angel Mounds">Angel Mounds</a> from about 900 A.D. to about 1600 A.D., just before the appearance of Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the abandonment of Angel Mounds between the years 1400 and 1450, tribes of <a href="/wiki/Miami_people" title="Miami people">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piankeshaw" title="Piankeshaw">Piankeshaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">Wyandot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Delaware</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> peoples were known to be in the area. The land encompassing Evansville was formally relinquished by the <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Delaware</a> in 1805 to <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">General William Henry Harrison</a>, then governor of the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Territory" title="Indiana Territory">Indiana Territory</a>. French hunters and trappers were among the first Europeans to come to the area, using <a href="/wiki/Vincennes,_Indiana" title="Vincennes, Indiana">Vincennes</a> as a base of operations.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="329" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Evans.jpg/150px-Evans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Evans.jpg/225px-Evans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Evans.jpg/300px-Evans.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Robert Morgan Evans</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 27, 1812, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_McGary_Jr." title="Hugh McGary Jr.">Hugh McGary Jr.</a> purchased about 441 acres and named it "McGary's Landing". In 1814, to attract more people, McGary renamed his village "Evansville" in honor of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morgan_Evans" title="Robert Morgan Evans">Colonel Robert Morgan Evans</a>. Evansville incorporated in 1817 and became a county seat on January 7, 1818. The county was named for Henry Vanderburgh, a deceased chief judge of the Indiana territorial supreme court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patry_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Patry-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morlock_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morlock-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville soon became a thriving commercial town with an extensive river trade, and the town began to expand outside of its original footprint. The west side of Evansville was for many years cut off from the main part of the city by <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Creek_(Indiana)" title="Pigeon Creek (Indiana)">Pigeon Creek</a> and the wide swath of factories that made the creek an important industrial corridor. The land comprising the former town of <a href="/wiki/Lamasco" title="Lamasco">Lamasco</a> was platted in 1837 and was ultimately annexed in 1870.</p>
<p>Evansville's economy received a boost in the early 1830s when Indiana unveiled plans to build the <a href="/wiki/Wabash_and_Erie_Canal" title="Wabash and Erie Canal">longest canal in the world</a>, a 400-mile ditch connecting the Great Lakes at <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Ohio" title="Toledo, Ohio">Toledo, Ohio</a> with the inland rivers at Evansville. The project was intended to open Indiana to commerce and improve transportation from <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. Unfortunately the project bankrupted the state and was so poorly engineered that it would not hold water. By the time the <a href="/wiki/Wabash_and_Erie_Canal" title="Wabash and Erie Canal">Wabash and Erie Canal</a> was finished in 1853, Evansville's first railroad, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evansville_%26_Crawfordsville_Railroad" title="Evansville &amp; Crawfordsville Railroad">Evansville &amp; Crawfordsville Railroad</a>, was opened to Terre Haute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorlock_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorlock-11">[11]</a></sup> Railroads had made the canal obsolete. Only two flat barges ever made the entire trip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evansville_Living_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evansville_Living-12">[12]</a></sup> The canal basin at Fifth and Court street in downtown Evansville eventually became the site of a new courthouse in 1891.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evansville_Living_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Evansville_Living-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The era of Evansville's greatest growth occurred in the second half of the 19th century, following the disruptions of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a>. The city was a major stop for steamboats along the Ohio River, and it was the home port for a number of companies engaged in trade via the river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Coal mining, manufacturing, and hardwood lumber was a major source of economic activity. By 1900 Evansville was one of the largest hardwood furniture centers in the world, with 41 factories employing approximately 2,000 workers. Eventually railroads became more important and in 1887 the <a href="/wiki/Louisville_and_Nashville_Railroad" title="Louisville and Nashville Railroad">L&amp;N Railroad</a> constructed a bridge across the Ohio River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> along with a major rail yard southwest of Evansville in a town, Howell, which was annexed in 1916 and completed the city's counterclockwise march around the horseshoe bend.</p>
<p>Throughout this period Evansville's main ethnic groups consisted of Germans fleeing Europe, Protestant Scotch-Irish from the South, Catholic Irish coming for canal or railroad work, New England businessmen, and newly freed slaves from Western Kentucky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> By the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Census,_1890" title="United States Census, 1890">U.S. census of 1890</a> Evansville ranked as the 56th largest urban area in the United States, a rank it gradually fell from in the early 1900s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> As the new century began, growth in the city continued to move eastward. Manufacturing also took off, particularly in the automobile and refrigeration industries.</p>
<p>The city saw exponential growth in the early twentieth century with production of lumber and the manufacturing of furniture. By 1920, there were more than two dozen furniture companies in Evansville. In the decades of the 1920s and 1930s city leaders attempted to improve Evansville's transportation position and successfully lobbied to be located on the Chicago-to-Miami "Dixie Bee Highway" (<a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_41_in_Indiana" title="U.S. Route 41 in Indiana">U.S. Highway 41</a>). A bridge was built across the Ohio River in 1932 and in that same decade steps were first taken to develop an airport. However, in 1937 a <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River_flood_of_1937" title="Ohio River flood of 1937">massive flood</a> covering 500 city blocks proved to be a major crises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> With steamboats less of a factor in the local economy, city and federal officials responded to the flood with about fifty years of levee construction that penned and hid the Ohio River behind a barrier of earthen berms and concrete walls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="1280" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg/220px-P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg/330px-P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg/440px-P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P-47D-40_Thunderbolt_44-95471_side.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
P-47 Thunderbolt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Evansville was a major center of industrial production and, as a result, it helped wipe away the last lingering effects of the Great Depression. A huge 45 acre shipyard complex was constructed on the riverfront east of St. Joseph Avenue for the production of oceangoing LSTs (<a href="/wiki/Landing_Ship,_Tank" title="Landing Ship, Tank">Landing Ship-Tanks</a>). The Evansville Shipyard was the nation's largest inland producer of LSTs. The Plymouth factory was converted into a plant which turned out "bullets by the billions," and many other companies switched over to the manufacture of war material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1942 the city acquired a factory adjacent to the airport north of the city for the manufacture of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P-47_Thunderbolt" title="P-47 Thunderbolt">P-47 Thunderbolt</a> fighter aircraft, known as the P-47Ds. Evansville produced a total 6,242 P-47s, almost half of the P47s made during the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war, Evansville's manufacturing base of automobiles, household appliances, and farm equipment benefited from growing post-war demand. A growing housing demand also caused residential development to leap north and east of the city. However, between 1955 and 1963 a nationwide recession hit Evansville particularly hard. Among other closures Servel (which produced refrigerators) went out of business and Chrysler terminated its local operations. The economy was saved from near total collapse by 28 businesses that moved into the area, including <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool_Corporation" title="Whirlpool Corporation">Whirlpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a>.</p>
<p>During the final third of the 20th century, Evansville became the commercial, medical, and service hub for the tri-state region. A 1990s economic spurt was fueled by the growth of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Indiana" title="University of Southern Indiana">University of Southern Indiana</a>. The arrival of giant <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Manufacturing_Indiana" title="Toyota Motor Manufacturing Indiana">Toyota</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AK_Steel_Holding_Corporation" title="AK Steel Holding Corporation">AK Steel</a> manufacturing plants, as well as <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Evansville" title="Tropicana Evansville">Tropicana Evansville</a>, Indiana's first gaming boat, also contributed to the growth of jobs. As the twenty-first century began, Evansville continued in a steady pace of economic diversification and stability.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="480" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif/250px-EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif/375px-EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/43/EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EvansvilleMSA-Census04.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Evansville Owensboro Metropolitan Areas. The Evansville Metropolitan Area includes Vanderburgh, Warrick, Henderson, Posey, Gibson, and Webster counties.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evansville-sky-view.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="864" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Evansville-sky-view.jpg/350px-Evansville-sky-view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Evansville-sky-view.jpg/525px-Evansville-sky-view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Evansville-sky-view.jpg/700px-Evansville-sky-view.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evansville-sky-view.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of the Evansville downtown region from the sky</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Evansville,_IN%E2%80%93KY_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Evansville, IN–KY Metropolitan Statistical Area">Evansville Metropolitan Area</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_metropolitan_statistical_areas_by_population" title="List of United States metropolitan statistical areas by population">142nd largest</a> in the United States, includes four <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_(US)" title="County (US)">counties</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gibson_County,_Indiana" title="Gibson County, Indiana">Gibson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Posey_County,_Indiana" title="Posey County, Indiana">Posey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanderburgh_County" title="Vanderburgh County">Vanderburgh</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warrick_County" title="Warrick County">Warrick</a>) and two <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> counties (<a href="/wiki/Henderson_County,_Kentucky" title="Henderson County, Kentucky">Henderson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Webster_County,_Kentucky" title="Webster County, Kentucky">Webster</a>). The metropolitan area does not include <a href="/wiki/Owensboro,_Kentucky" title="Owensboro, Kentucky">Owensboro, Kentucky</a>, which is an adjacent metropolitan area about 30 miles (48 km) southeast of Evansville. This area is sometimes referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Evansville,_IN%E2%80%93KY_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Evansville, IN–KY Metropolitan Statistical Area">Kentuckiana</a>", although the area is usually referred to as the "Tri-State" by the local media.Evansville is located at 37°58'38" north, 87°33'2" west (37.977166, −87.550566).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-21">[21]</a></sup> According to the 2010 census, Evansville has a total area of 44.622 square miles (115.57 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 44.15 square miles (114.35 km<sup>2</sup>) (or 98.94%) is land and 0.472 square miles (1.22 km<sup>2</sup>) (or 1.06%) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census-g001_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-g001-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's southern boundary lies on an oxbow in the Ohio River. Most of the city lies in a shallow valley surrounded by low rolling hills. The west side of the city is built on these rolling hills and is home to <a href="/wiki/Burdette_Park" title="Burdette Park">Burdette Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesker_Amphitheatre" title="Mesker Amphitheatre">Mesker Amphitheatre</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesker_Park_Zoo" title="Mesker Park Zoo">Mesker Park Zoo</a>. The eastern portion of the city developed in the valley and is protected by a series of levees that closely follow the path of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_164" title="Interstate 164">I164-69</a>. Notable landmarks on the east side are the 240-acre (1.0 km<sup>2</sup>) <a href="/wiki/Wesselman_Woods_Nature_Preserve" title="Wesselman Woods Nature Preserve">Wesselman Woods Nature Preserve</a> and the Angel Mounds State Historic Site, located just southeast of Evansville, between Evansville and <a href="/wiki/Newburgh,_Indiana" title="Newburgh, Indiana">Newburgh</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Evansville" title="List of tallest buildings in Evansville">List of tallest buildings in Evansville</a></i></p>
<p>Evansville's original <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Evansville" title="Downtown Evansville">downtown plat</a> was made on about 200 acres, with streets running parallel to the river from northwest to southeast. Other streets nearby were later laid out on the cardinal points, due north-south and east-west. Thus, anyone entering or leaving downtown finds that the street makes a confusing oblique-angle turn in one direction or another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In the 1970s, the city suffered from problems such as decreased economic activity and suburban flight, but city-sponsored revitalization has since improved downtown conditions.</p>
<p>The business district and riverfront features riverboat gambling, restaurants, bars, and shops, attracting tens of thousands of visitors each year. Although much of the outer city's architecture is typical suburban design, <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Evansville" title="Downtown Evansville">the city's downtown district</a> still retains quite a bit of early twentieth century architecture. Just a few blocks east of the main business district is the <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Historic_District_(Evansville,_Indiana)" title="Riverside Historic District (Evansville, Indiana)">Riverside district</a> featuring tree-lined brick streets full of turn of the twentieth century homes. The <a href="/wiki/Reitz_Home_Museum" title="Reitz Home Museum">Reitz Home Museum</a> is one of the finest examples of French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Empire_(architecture)" title="Second Empire (architecture)">Second Empire</a> architecture in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Other homes nearby feature similar character and design and include <a href="/wiki/Italianate_architecture" title="Italianate architecture">Italianate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Revival_architecture" title="Colonial Revival architecture">Colonial Revival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Renaissance Revival</a> styles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">Neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Evansville has thirteen neighborhoods that have qualified for the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Evansville lies in the northern reaches of a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cfa</i>), and straddles the border between <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">USDA Plant Hardiness Zones</a> 6b and 7a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Summers are hot and humid, winters are cool to cold. Average temperatures range from 32.5 °F (0.3 °C) in January to 78.0 °F (25.6 °C) in July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-25">[25]</a></sup> Annual rainfall averages 45.3 inches (1,150 mm) and seasonal snowfall averages 11.8 inches (30 cm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Evansville winters can range from just 0.5 in (1.3 cm) of snowfall in 2011–12, up to 37.9 in (96 cm) in 1969–70.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Extreme temperatures range from −23 °F (−31 °C) on February 2, 1951 up to 111 °F (44 °C) on July 28, 1930.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FactFinder_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FactFinder-3">[3]</a></sup> of 2010, there were 117,429 people, 50,588 households, and 28,085 families residing in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 2,659.8 inhabitants per square mile (1,027.0/km<sup>2</sup>). There were 57,799 housing units at an average density of 1,309.2 per square mile (505.5/km<sup>2</sup>). The racial makeup of the city was 82.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">White</a>, 12.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">African American</a>, 0.3% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">Native American</a>, 1.0% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>, 0.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">Pacific Islander</a>, 1.3% from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">other races</a>, and 2.8% from two or more races. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race were 2.6% of the population.</p>
<p>There were 50,588 households of which 27.6% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 34.8% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 15.6% had a female householder with no husband present, 5.2% had a male householder with no wife present, and 44.5% were non-families. 36.5% of all households were made up of individuals and 11.9% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.23 and the average family size was 2.91.</p>
<p>The median age in the city was 36.5 years. 22.1% of residents were under the age of 18; 11.7% were between the ages of 18 and 24; 26% were from 25 to 44; 25.8% were from 45 to 64; and 14.4% were 65 years of age or older. The gender makeup of the city was 48.1% male and 51.9% female.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Evansville is the regional center for a large trade area in <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>. The broad economic base of the region has helped build an economy which is known for its stability, diversity, and vitality. The largest industry sectors by size in Evansville are health care, finance, education, and manufacturing. Other major industries by employment are energy, warehousing and distribution, and retail.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evilleriverfront.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evilleriverfront.jpg/250px-Evilleriverfront.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evilleriverfront.jpg/375px-Evilleriverfront.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Evilleriverfront.jpg/500px-Evilleriverfront.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evilleriverfront.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The downtown riverfront area features tiered stadium seating for special events and fireworks along the Ohio River.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Corporate headquarters located in Evansville include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accuride" title="Accuride">Accuride</a>, Ameriqual Group, Anchor Industries, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Van_Lines" title="Atlas Van Lines">Atlas Van Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berry_Plastics" title="Berry Plastics">Berry Plastics</a>, Evana Tool &amp; Engineering, <a href="/wiki/Karges_Furniture" title="Karges Furniture">Karges Furniture</a>, Koch Enterprises, Lewis Bakeries, Metronet, <a href="/wiki/Old_National_Bank" title="Old National Bank">Old National Bank</a>, Red Spot Paint &amp; Varnish, <a href="/wiki/Shoe_Carnival" title="Shoe Carnival">Shoe Carnival</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Springleaf" title="Springleaf">Springleaf Financial</a>, Traylor Brothers, and <a href="/wiki/Vectren" title="Vectren">Vectren</a>. Major manufacturing operations near the city include <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Newburgh,_Indiana" title="Newburgh, Indiana">Newburgh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AK_Steel_Holding_Corporation" title="AK Steel Holding Corporation">AK Steel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rockport,_Indiana" title="Rockport, Indiana">Rockport</a>, <a href="/wiki/SABIC" title="SABIC">SABIC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon,_Indiana" title="Mount Vernon, Indiana">Mount Vernon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Manufacturing_Indiana" title="Toyota Motor Manufacturing Indiana">Toyota</a> in <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_Indiana" title="Princeton, Indiana">Princeton</a>. Other major employers with workforces of 500 or more in the area include <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol-Myers_Squibb" title="Bristol-Myers Squibb">Bristol-Myers Squibb</a>, <a href="/wiki/SRG_Global" title="SRG Global">SRG Global</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skanska" title="Skanska">Industrial Contractors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mead_Johnson" title="Mead Johnson">Mead Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Energy" title="Peabody Energy">Peabody Energy</a>, PGW Pittsburgh Glass, <a href="/wiki/T.J._Maxx" title="T.J. Maxx">T.J. Maxx</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Evansville" title="Tropicana Evansville">Tropicana Evansville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville has emerged as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illinois%E2%80%93Indiana%E2%80%93Kentucky_tri-state_area" title="Illinois–Indiana–Kentucky tri-state area">tri-state</a>'s major center for the health care and medical sciences industries. <a href="/wiki/Deaconess_Hospital_(Evansville,_Indiana)" title="Deaconess Hospital (Evansville, Indiana)">Deaconess Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Hospital_and_Medical_Center" title="St. Mary's Hospital and Medical Center">St. Mary's Hospital and Medical Center</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Deaconess_Gateway_and_Women%27s_Hospital" title="Deaconess Gateway and Women's Hospital">Deaconess Gateway and Women's Hospital</a> located just outside city limits, provide the anchors for a vast health care system that are also among the region's largest employers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Educational institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_School_Corporation" title="Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation">Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Tech_Community_College_of_Indiana" title="Ivy Tech Community College of Indiana">Ivy Tech Community College of Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">University of Evansville</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Indiana" title="University of Southern Indiana">University of Southern Indiana</a> also contribute thousands of jobs to the tri-state annually.</p>
<p>Evansville's strategic location on the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>, strong rail and highway infrastructure, and its designation as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Customs" title="United States Customs">U.S. Customs Port of Entry</a>, make it an ideal location for the transfer of cargo, including internationally. Chemicals make up 64% of international exports from the metro area, followed by transportation equipment (18%) and food manufacturing (5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville is also known as a regional energy hub due to the headquarters of Vectren and regional energy-related facilities such as <a href="/wiki/Babcock_%26_Wilcox" title="Babcock &amp; Wilcox">Babcock &amp; Wilcox</a>'s Nuclear Operations Group, numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_industry" title="Coal industry">coal mines</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.gbtholding.com/" rel="nofollow">Global Blade Technology</a>, several large <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a> facilities, and a robust network of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> pipelines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Evansville is a partner in <a class="external text" href="http://www.indianaprojectgreen.org" rel="nofollow">Project Green</a>, a regional economic development plan focused on the energy industry.</p>
<p>The city of Evansville offers a pro-business tax structure for companies locating inside the Evansville Urban Enterprise Zone. Established in 1984 as one of only five enterprise zones in the State of Indiana, the 2.1-square-mile (5.4 km<sup>2</sup>) Evansville Urban Enterprise Zone offers inventory tax credits and other tax credits to eligible businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_features">Cultural features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cultural features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_art_in_Evansville,_Indiana" title="List of public art in Evansville, Indiana">List of public art in Evansville, Indiana</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_venues">Entertainment venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Entertainment venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="710" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg/220px-Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg/330px-Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg/440px-Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bosse_Field_Lights.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bosse Field</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bosse_Field" title="Bosse Field">Historic Bosse Field</a>, a 7,180 seat baseball stadium located in Garvin Park, was built in 1915 and is the third-oldest ballpark still in regular use in the United States, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a> (1912) in Boston and <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> (1914) in Chicago.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6016" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg/220px-Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg/330px-Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg/440px-Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Center_from_Main_Street.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ford Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a> is a multi-use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indoor_arena" title="Indoor arena">indoor arena</a> downtown with a maximum seating capacity of 11,000 which will also be connected via Sky Bridge to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evansville_DoubleTree_Hotel" title="Evansville DoubleTree Hotel">Evansville DoubleTree Hotel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> It officially opened in 2011 as the city's premier entertainment venue and is mainly used for <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Concerts" title="Concerts">concerts</a>.</p>
<p>A wide variety of concerts, plays, conventions, expositions and other special events are held at the 2,500-seat auditorium and convention center at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Centre_(Evansville)" title="The Centre (Evansville)">The Old National Events Plaza</a> downtown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/220px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/330px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/440px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Victory Theatre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Victory_Theatre" title="Victory Theatre">Victory Theatre</a> is a vintage 1,950-seat venue that is home to the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Evansville Philharmonic Orchestra">Evansville Philharmonic Orchestra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Each year, the orchestra presents a seven-concert classics series, four double pops performances, and special event concerts, as well as numerous educational and outreach performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The theater also hosts local ballet and modern dance companies, theater companies, and touring productions.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">University of Evansville</a> maintains a prestigious theater program – one of the top rated programs in the nation, which features four mainstage and two studio productions a year. The University of Evansville has been honored more times at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Kennedy_Center" title="The Kennedy Center">The Kennedy Center</a> than any other theatre institution. The University is the only institution, along with Yale, which has been asked to perform at the Kennedy Center without first going through competition. It also leads the nation in the top awards for its students as awarded by The Broadway Theatre Wing and other governing bodies of serious theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Evansville Civic Theatre is Southern Indiana's longest running community theater, dating from the 1920s when the community theater movement swept across the country. From its humble beginnings at the old Central High School auditorium, Evansville Civic Theatre has had many homes – <a href="/wiki/Soldiers_and_Sailors_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Coliseum">Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Coliseum</a>, Bosse High School, the Rose Room of the McCurdy Hotel, the Elks Ballroom, and the Evansville Museum of Arts and Sciences. In 1974, Evansville Civic Theatre acquired the historic Columbia Movie Theater as its permanent home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_festivals">Annual festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Annual festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fall_fes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="293" data-file-width="450" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Fall_fes.jpg/220px-Fall_fes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Fall_fes.jpg/330px-Fall_fes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Fall_fes.jpg/440px-Fall_fes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fall_fes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Nut_Club_Fall_Festival" title="West Side Nut Club Fall Festival">West Side Nut Club Fall Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Nut_Club_Fall_Festival" title="West Side Nut Club Fall Festival">West Side Nut Club Fall Festival</a> is a street fair held in the area west of downtown Evansville. It is held on the first full week of October and draws between 100,000 and 150,000 people each day. The main attraction of the festival is the food, with offerings of standards like elephant ears and corn dogs to the more unusual, such as chocolate-covered crickets, <a href="/wiki/Fried-brain_sandwich" title="Fried-brain sandwich">brain sandwiches</a>, and alligator stew. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Harvey" title="Paul Harvey">Paul Harvey</a> once remarked that only <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras" title="Mardi Gras">Mardi Gras</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans</a> is larger than the Fall Festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each June the city plays host to the annual <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=ShrinersFest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="ShrinersFest (page does not exist)">ShrinersFest</a>. Frequently the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Blue_Angels" title="Blue Angels">Blue Angels</a> have been an attraction at this event, along with the Canadian Forces Snowbirds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Previously, from 1979 to 2009, Evansville hosted <a href="/wiki/Thunder_on_the_Ohio" title="Thunder on the Ohio">Thunder on the Ohio</a> as part of the Freedom Festival, which was a <a href="/wiki/Hydroplane_(boat)" title="Hydroplane (boat)">hydroplane</a> boat race in the <a href="/wiki/H1_Unlimited" title="H1 Unlimited">H1 Unlimited</a> season.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Germania_M%C3%A4nnerchor_Volksfest" title="Germania Männerchor Volksfest">Germania Männerchor Volksfest</a> is a three-day German heritage festival which takes place every August in the historic Germania Mannerchor building on the city's west side. The festival includes food, drink, dance and music. Many of the city's residents with German ancestry also wear historic German attire. On the last weekend of August, the popular 4,000 street rods converge on the Vanderburgh County 4-H fairgrounds north of the city for "Frog Follies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reitzhome.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Reitzhome.jpg/220px-Reitzhome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Reitzhome.jpg/330px-Reitzhome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5e/Reitzhome.jpg/440px-Reitzhome.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reitzhome.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The historic <a href="/wiki/Reitz_Home_Museum" title="Reitz Home Museum">Reitz Home Museum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Angel_Mounds" title="Angel Mounds">Angel Mounds State Historic Site</a> is nationally recognized as one of the best preserved prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> sites in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> From 1100 to 1450 A. D., a town near this site was home to people of the Middle Mississippian culture. Several thousand people lived in this town protected by a stockade made of wattle and daub. Because Angel Mounds was a <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">chiefdom</a> (the home of the chief), it was the regional center of a large community.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Evansville" title="Children's Museum of Evansville">The Children's Museum of Evansville</a> opened its doors to the public in September 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The museum is the result of two years of planning and was constructed in the historic Central Library downtown. The <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> building is listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>. The museum offers visitors three floors of interactive exhibits and galleries.</p>
<p>The Evansville African American Museum was established to continually develop a resource and cultural center to collect, preserve, and educate the public on the history and traditions of African American families, organizations, and communities. The museum is located in the last remaining building of Lincoln Gardens, the second Federal Housing Project created under the administration of Franklin D. Roosevelt’s New Deal in 1938.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Museum_of_Arts,_History_and_Science" title="Evansville Museum of Arts, History and Science">Evansville Museum of Arts, History and Science</a> is home to one of southern Indiana's most established and significant cultural centers. It holds the Koch Planetarium, the oldest in Indiana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Also on the campus is the Evansville Museum Transportation Center, which features transportation in southern Indiana from the latter part of the Nineteenth Century through the mid-Twentieth Century.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reitz_Home_Museum" title="Reitz Home Museum">Reitz Home Museum</a> is Evansville's only Victorian House Museum. It is noted as one of the country's finest examples of <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">Second French Empire</a> architecture. It was placed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> in 1973.</p>
<p>In October 2005 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_LST_325" title="USS LST 325">USS LST 325</a> moored in Evansville and was turned into a museum (USS LST Ship Memorial) in recognition of the city's war effort. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Evansville produced 167 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank_landing_ship" title="Tank landing ship">LSTs</a> (and 35 other craft), making it the largest inland producer of LSTs in the nation. The USS LST 325 is the last navigable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank_landing_ship" title="Tank landing ship">tank landing ship</a> in operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mesker_Park_Zoo">Mesker Park Zoo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mesker Park Zoo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesker_Park_Zoo" title="Mesker Park Zoo">The Mesker Park Zoo &amp; Botanic Garden</a> opened in 1928 and is one of the oldest and largest zoos in the state. Set in a 50-acre (200,000 m<sup>2</sup>) park, the zoo features 200 species and more than 700 animals roaming freely in natural habitats surrounded by exotic plants, wildflowers, and trees, including the Amazonia exhibit which opened in 2008. An estimated 3 million people visit the zoo between April and August every year. Mesker Park Zoo is accredited by the Association of Zoos and Aquariums. The zoo regularly hosts events such as Boo at the Zoo, Breakfast with Santa and Fun in the Forest throughout the year.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_Evansville" title="Sports in Evansville">Sports in Evansville</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UE_awards.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UE_awards.jpg/220px-UE_awards.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UE_awards.jpg/330px-UE_awards.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UE_awards.jpg/440px-UE_awards.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UE_awards.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The memorial display case at the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a> honoring UE's championship tradition</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Evansville has a long and rich history supporting athletic teams and events, with a number of notable professional athletes coming from the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">High school</a> athletics are a frequent source of local patronage, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">University of Evansville</a> (UE) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Indiana" title="University of Southern Indiana">University of Southern Indiana</a> (USI) regularly draw thousands of spectators to NCAA Division I and Division II sporting events, respectively. The UE <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Purple_Aces" title="Evansville Purple Aces">Purple Aces</a> basketball team plays at the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a>. USI plays on campus at the USI Physical Activities Center.</p>
<p>Evansville is home to several semi-professional and professional teams as well. The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Otters" title="Evansville Otters">Evansville Otters</a> are a professional baseball team in the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_League" title="Frontier League">Frontier League</a> and have played at historic <a href="/wiki/Bosse_Field" title="Bosse Field">Bosse Field</a> since 1995. The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Thunderbolts" title="Evansville Thunderbolts">Evansville Thunderbolts</a> are a minor league professional <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Professional_Hockey_League" title="Southern Professional Hockey League">Southern Professional Hockey League</a> and play at the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Crush" title="Evansville Crush">Evansville Crush</a> is a semi-professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> team in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_Arena_Soccer_League" title="Premier Arena Soccer League">PASL</a>. The Evansvile Enforcers are a semi-professional <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team in the Kentucky Football League League. There is also a junior hockey team named the Evansville Jr. Thunderbolts in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_3_Hockey_League" title="North American 3 Hockey League">NA3HL</a> and play at the <a href="/wiki/Swonder_Ice_Arena" title="Swonder Ice Arena">Swonder Ice Arena</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Soldiers_and_Sailors_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Coliseum">Evansville Coliseum</a> is home to the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Flat_Track_Derby_Association" title="Women's Flat Track Derby Association">WFTDA</a> league, the <a href="/wiki/Demolition_City_Roller_Derby" title="Demolition City Roller Derby">Demolition City Roller Derby</a>.</p>

<p>From 1957 to 1975, and then again in 2002 and 2014, Evansville hosted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_II_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division II Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Division II Basketball Championship</a> (Elite Eight). From 1999 to 2007, <a href="/wiki/Roberts_Municipal_Stadium" title="Roberts Municipal Stadium">Roberts Stadium</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Valley_Conference" title="Great Lakes Valley Conference">Great Lakes Valley Conference</a> basketball tournaments, and in 2013 the same event was held at the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Center_(Evansville)" title="Ford Center (Evansville)">Ford Center</a>. A number of Division I NCAA events have been hosted by the city as well. In 1983 <a href="/wiki/Roberts_Municipal_Stadium" title="Roberts Municipal Stadium">Roberts Stadium</a> hosted the first round of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship</a>, and in 1980 and 1983 it hosted the <a href="/wiki/Horizon_League" title="Horizon League">Midwestern City Conference</a> men's basketball conference tournament.</p>
<p>Evansville used to play host to the top tier boat racing circuit of <a href="/wiki/H1_Unlimited" title="H1 Unlimited">H1 Unlimited</a> when it hosted <a href="/wiki/Thunder_on_the_Ohio" title="Thunder on the Ohio">Thunder on the Ohio</a> along the Ohio River in downtown Evansville, which was hosted continuously from 1979 to 2009. Evansville had also previously hosted Thunder on the Ohio from 1938 to 1940. The 2 mile Evansville tri-oval was known as one of the fastest hyrdroplane courses in the world, as various world records were set on the Evansville course.</p>
<p>Evansville offers modern sports facilities for both soccer and ice skating events. The <a href="/wiki/Goebel_Soccer_Complex" title="Goebel Soccer Complex">Goebel Soccer Complex</a> is on 70 acres (280,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of land and features nine Olympic-size irrigated Bermuda grass fields and one Olympic-size AstroPlay turf field. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/EVSC_Fields" title="EVSC Fields">EVSC Fields</a> provide twin soccer fields and stadium seating for high school regular season and postseason matches. <a href="/wiki/Swonder_Ice_Arena" title="Swonder Ice Arena">Swonder Ice Arena</a> is a double-rink facility that opened in the fall of 2002 and features a fitness center, a skate park, and party rooms. The schools of the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_School_Corporation" title="Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation">Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation</a> use. Lloyd Pool for all of their swimming and diving meets in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Indiana_Athletic_Conference" title="Southern Indiana Athletic Conference">Southern Indiana Athletic Conference</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Four_Freedoms_Monument,_Evansville,_Indiana.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG/220px-Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG/330px-Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG/440px-Four_Freedoms_Monument%2C_Evansville%2C_Indiana.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Four_Freedoms_Monument,_Evansville,_Indiana.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Four Freedoms Monument along the Ohio River.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wesselman_Woods_Nature_Preserve" title="Wesselman Woods Nature Preserve">Wesselman Woods Nature Preserve</a> is a <a href="/wiki/National_Natural_Landmark" title="National Natural Landmark">National Natural Landmark</a> with nearly 200 acres (0.8 km<sup>2</sup>) of virgin bottomland hardwood forest. It is the largest tract of virgin forest located inside any city limits within the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The Nature Center features exhibits, events, wildlife observation areas, meeting rooms, library, and gift shop. Adjacent to the Nature Preserve, Wesselman Park features a Par 3 golf course, basketball courts, tennis courts, sand volleyball courts, softball fields, and a playground; and Roberts Park is a proposed, adjacent park on the former site of Roberts Stadium,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-49">[49]</a></sup> though funding for Roberts Park and an expansion to the parks system remains unresolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin2_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin2-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville has an extensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_park" title="Municipal park">municipal park</a> system with 65 parks and 21 special facilities encompassing more than 2,300 acres (9 km<sup>2</sup>) of land in the city of Evansville and Vanderburgh County. A growing bicycle and pedestrian trail extends into adjacent counties and ties into the <a href="/wiki/American_Discovery_Trail" title="American Discovery Trail">American Discovery Trail</a>. This trail system includes the <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_Creek_(Indiana)" title="Pigeon Creek (Indiana)">Pigeon Creek Greenway Passage</a>, a 42-mile trail that encircles the city. Access to the completed portions of the trail are found at Garvin Park (N. Main Street and Heidelbach Ave.) and at the downtown Riverfront. The city's parks department also operates two Par 4 18-hole public <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> courses, 1 Par 3 18-hole course, one Par 4 9-hole golf course, two disc golf courses, Garvin Park, Lloyd Pool, the Goebel Soccer Complex, Swonder Ice Arena and the C.K. Newsome Community Center.</p>
<p>Anchored by the <a href="/wiki/Four_Freedoms" title="Four Freedoms">Four Freedoms</a> Monument and the <a href="/wiki/Tropicana_Evansville" title="Tropicana Evansville">Tropicana Evansville</a>, Dress Plaza along the riverfront offers a brick paved walkway above, and tiered seating below provide a view of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>. Convenient driving access with parking is available along the lower plaza that is the scene for numerous summer concerts and festivals.</p>
<p>Located on nearly 200 acres (0.8 km<sup>2</sup>) of rolling hills in western Vanderburgh County well outside of the city limits, <a href="/wiki/Burdette_Park" title="Burdette Park">Burdette Park</a> features an aquatic center with water slides, three pools, and a snack bar. It also offers a BMX racing track, batting cages, softball diamonds, miniature golf, tennis courts, and locations for fishing.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg/220px-Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg/330px-Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg/440px-Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Willard_Carpenter_House_front.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
WNIN's headquarters at the <a href="/wiki/Willard_Carpenter_House" title="Willard Carpenter House">Willard Carpenter House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Evansville_Courier_%26_Press" title="Evansville Courier &amp; Press">Evansville Courier &amp; Press</a></i>, owned by the Journal Media Group, serves the Evansville area. The newspaper also publishes the monthly magazines <i><a class="external text" href="http://www.ebj.biz" rel="nofollow">Evansville Business Journal</a></i> and <i>eWoman Magazine</i>, and it owns the <i><a href="/wiki/Henderson_Gleaner" title="Henderson Gleaner">Henderson Gleaner</a></i> in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Henderson,_Kentucky" title="Henderson, Kentucky">Henderson, Kentucky</a>. <i><a class="external text" href="http://www.evansvilleliving.com" rel="nofollow">Evansville Living</a></i> and <i><a class="external text" href="http://www.evansvillebusiness.com" rel="nofollow">Evansville Business</a></i>, published locally by Tucker Publishing Group, are bi-monthly local magazines showcasing the people, businesses, and communities in the area. Other media publications include <i>Maturity Journal</i>, a free monthly newspaper aimed at senior citizens, and <i><a class="external text" href="http://news4uonline.com" rel="nofollow">News4U</a></i>, a free monthly entertainment magazine.</p>
<p>The Evansville area is primarily serviced by radio stations in Indiana and Kentucky. The two main radio groups in Evansville that control the majority of its radio stations are <a href="/wiki/Townsquare_Media" title="Townsquare Media">Townsquare Media</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midwest_Communications" title="Midwest Communications">Midwest Communications</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Radio stations providing coverage to Evansville include:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><a href="/wiki/WSWI" title="WSWI">WSWI/820</a>, <a href="/wiki/WGBF_(AM)" title="WGBF (AM)">WGBF/1280</a>, <a href="/wiki/WBGW_(AM)" title="WBGW (AM)">WBGW/1330</a>, <a href="/wiki/WEOA" title="WEOA">WEOA/1400</a>, <a href="/wiki/WABX" title="WABX">WABX/107.5</a>, <a href="/wiki/WDKS" title="WDKS">WDKS/106.1</a>, <a href="/wiki/WJPS" title="WJPS">WJPS/107.1</a>, <a href="/wiki/WGBF-FM" title="WGBF-FM">WGBF-FM/103.1</a>, <a href="/wiki/WIKY-FM" title="WIKY-FM">WIKY-FM/104.1</a>, <a href="/wiki/WJLT" title="WJLT">WJLT/105.3</a>, <a href="/wiki/WKDQ" title="WKDQ">WKDQ/99.5</a>, <a href="/wiki/WLFW" title="WLFW">WLFW/93.5</a>, <a href="/wiki/WNIN-FM" title="WNIN-FM">WNIN-FM/88.3</a>, <a href="/wiki/WSTO" title="WSTO">WSTO/96.1</a>, <a href="/wiki/WBKR" title="WBKR">WBKR/92.5</a> <a href="/wiki/WUEV" title="WUEV">WUEV/91.5</a> and <a href="/wiki/WPSR_(FM)" title="WPSR (FM)">WPSR/90.7</a>.</p>
<p>Evansville is, as of the 2015-16 rankings, the 103rd-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_North_America_by_media_market" title="List of television stations in North America by media market">television market</a> in the United States according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Media_Research" title="Nielsen Media Research">Nielsen Media Research</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" title="Designated market area">designated market area</a> consists of 30 counties in Southeastern <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Indiana" title="Southwestern Indiana">Southwestern Indiana</a>, and Northwestern <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>. The 2010 population estimate of this 30-county region is nearly one million people.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">Law and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Law and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="897" data-file-width="731" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg/220px-Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg/330px-Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg/440px-Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lloyd-carol-winnecke.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Current Evansville Mayor <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Winnecke" title="Lloyd Winnecke">Lloyd Winnecke</a> and his wife Carol on election night, November 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mayor of Evansville, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Winnecke" title="Lloyd Winnecke">Lloyd Winnecke</a>, serves as the chief executive officer. Indiana has what is called a "strong mayor" system, so the mayor has most of the executive and administrative power over the city’s daily operations. A nine-member elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Council" title="City Council">City Council</a> is the legislative and fiscal body of city government. The Council’s nine members are made up of one representative from each of the City’s six Council districts and three at-large members. Members are part-time elected officials who serve for four-year terms. As the legislative body, the Council has the exclusive responsibility of passing or changing local laws. As the fiscal body, the Council has the authority to levy certain taxes and it has the sole responsibility of adopting a City budget each year.</p>
