<p>The Evansville Police Department, founded in 1863, is the city's <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement" title="Law enforcement">law enforcement</a> agency. Prior to that, law enforcement was the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Warrick_County,_Indiana" title="Warrick County, Indiana">Warrick County</a> <a href="/wiki/Sheriff" title="Sheriff">sheriff</a> (1818 to 1847) and the city marshal (1847 to 1863). From 1863 to 1883, the city marshal shared policing duties with the police department. The current chief of police Billy Bolin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The county has eight state trial courts of original jurisdiction. One circuit court and seven superior courts. The judges offices are non-partisan with terms of six years. A judge must be a member of the Indiana Bar Association. The judges are assisted by magistrates that are appointed. <a href="/wiki/Circuit_court" title="Circuit court">circuit court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inc2102_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-inc2102-57">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Southern_District_of_Indiana" title="United States District Court for the Southern District of Indiana">United States District Court for the Southern District of Indiana</a> maintains a permanent division in the city.</p>
<p>Vanderburgh County's delegation to the Indiana State House of Representatives comprises three representatives: Wendy McNamara (District 76), <a href="/wiki/Gail_Riecken" title="Gail Riecken">Gail Riecken</a> (District 77), and Holli Sullivan (District 78). Evansville and Vanderburgh County are represented by two state senators. In general, the southern third of the county and Armstrong Township are part of District 49, currently held by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Tomes" title="Jim Tomes">Jim Tomes</a>. The county's west side is also in District 49. Most of the county is in District 50, which extends to the east, a seat held by <a href="/wiki/Vaneta_Becker" title="Vaneta Becker">Vaneta Becker</a>.</p>
<p>The region is located in the <a href="/wiki/Indiana%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Indiana's 8th congressional district">8th District of Indiana</a> (<a class="external text" href="http://nationalatlas.gov/printable/images/preview/congdist/in08_109.gif" rel="nofollow">map</a>) and served by U.S. Representative <a href="/wiki/Larry_Bucshon" title="Larry Bucshon">Larry Bucshon</a>.</p>
<p>Evansville is the county seat for <a href="/wiki/Vanderburgh_County,_Indiana" title="Vanderburgh County, Indiana">Vanderburgh County</a>. Some of the city's governmental functions are shared with <a href="/wiki/Vanderburgh_County,_Indiana" title="Vanderburgh County, Indiana">Vanderburgh County</a> officials. In recent years various bi-partisan groups have advocated merging the Evansville city and Vanderburgh County governments, as was done in other surrounding cities such as <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Evansville and Vanderburgh County already have a number of notable merged government functions. The school system is consolidated county wide in the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_School_Corporation" title="Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation">Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation</a> and the library system is consolidated countywide in the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_Public_Library" title="Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library">Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library</a>. Additional countywide authorities are in place for the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Regional_Airport" title="Evansville Regional Airport">Evansville Regional Airport</a> and for flood control via the countywide levee authority.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UE1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/UE1.JPG/220px-UE1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/UE1.JPG/330px-UE1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/UE1.JPG/440px-UE1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UE1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UE's front oval</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ricelibrary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Ricelibrary.jpg/220px-Ricelibrary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Ricelibrary.jpg/330px-Ricelibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Ricelibrary.jpg/440px-Ricelibrary.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ricelibrary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
USI's Rice Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Evansville is home to several institutions of higher learning. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Evansville" title="University of Evansville">University of Evansville</a> (UE) is a small, private, <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">Methodist affiliated</a> university with approximately 3,050 students. Founded in 1854, UE features <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_arts" title="Liberal arts">liberal arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a> degrees along with a nationally renowned theatre department. Nearly half of UE's students study abroad as part of their experience, including at a satellite campus, <a href="/wiki/Harlaxton_Manor" title="Harlaxton Manor">Harlaxton College</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Grantham" title="Grantham">Grantham</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. UE athletic teams participate in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> and are known as the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Purple_Aces" title="Evansville Purple Aces">Purple Aces</a>. Evansville is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Valley_Conference" title="Missouri Valley Conference">Missouri Valley Conference</a></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Indiana" title="University of Southern Indiana">University of Southern Indiana</a> (USI) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public university</a> located just outside Evansville city limits. Founded in 1965, the school has an enrollment of over 10,800 students and is among the fastest growing comprehensive state universities in Indiana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Southern_Indiana_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Southern_Indiana-59">[59]</a></sup> USI athletic teams participate in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">Division II</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> and are known as the Screaming Eagles. USI is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Valley_Conference" title="Great Lakes Valley Conference">Great Lakes Valley Conference</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Indiana_University_School_of_Medicine_-_Evansville" title="Indiana University School of Medicine - Evansville">Indiana University School of Medicine - Evansville</a> is currently housed on USI's campus, but there are plans to locate a new interdisciplinary academic health science education and research campus downtown. Other campuses in the city include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivy_Tech_Community_College" title="Ivy Tech Community College">Ivy Tech Community College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrison_College_(Indiana)" title="Harrison College (Indiana)">Harrison College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oakland_City_University" title="Oakland City University">Oakland City University</a>'s School of Adult and Extended Learning.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_education">Primary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Primary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/220px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/330px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg/440px-Victory_Theater_and_Hotel_Sonntag.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Signature_School" title="Signature School">Signature School</a> (previously the Sonntag Hotel) shares a building with the Victory Theatre</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg/220px-Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg/330px-Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg/440px-Reitz_Memorial_High_School.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<dl>
<dd><i>Also see: <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_School_Corporation" title="Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation">Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Evansville" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Evansville">Roman Catholic Diocese of Evansville</a></i> .</dd>
</dl>
<p>Evansville has one unified school system with the county, the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_School_Corporation" title="Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation">Evansville Vanderburgh School Corporation</a> (EVSC). It consists of five public high schools, 11 middle schools, and 20 elementary schools. In addition there are two parochial, two charter, and one private school. One charter school - <a href="/wiki/Signature_School" title="Signature School">Signature School</a> - attracts top tier students and is consistently ranked by a number of publications as one of the top high schools in the United States.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evpl-central.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="634" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Evpl-central.jpg/220px-Evpl-central.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Evpl-central.jpg/330px-Evpl-central.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Evpl-central.jpg/440px-Evpl-central.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evpl-central.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
EVPL's Central Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg/220px-Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg/330px-Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg/440px-Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Willard_Library_from_southwest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Willard_Library" title="Willard Library">Willard Library</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Evansville is home to an award-winning library system, the <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Vanderburgh_Public_Library" title="Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library">Evansville Vanderburgh Public Library</a> (EVPL). As a unified system serving both Evansville and the surrounding county, EVPL is one of the largest public library systems in <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> It was rated a five star library by the <a href="/wiki/Library_Journal" title="Library Journal">Library Journal</a>, which places it in the top 1% of public libraries in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> EVPL also obtained a Top Ten library ranking in the 2010 edition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hennen%27s_American_Public_Library_Ratings" title="Hennen's American Public Library Ratings">Hennen's American Public Library Ratings</a>, achieving a number eight ranking within its population category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>An independent private institution, <a href="/wiki/Willard_Library" title="Willard Library">Willard Library</a>, is also located within Evansville. Willard was formed in 1881 to serve the public, regardless of race, a very progressive mission in the latter half of the nineteenth century. The library houses a renowned trove of local archives and genealogical materials, in addition to its collection of standard publications. The building is constructed in the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival style</a> and was listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> in 1972.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weekend_education">Weekend education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Weekend education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Southern Indiana Japanese School (SJIS; 南インディアナ補習授業校 <i>Minami Indiana Hoshū Jugyō Kō</i>), a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hoshuko" title="Hoshuko">weekend Japanese school</a>, has its offices and classrooms at Nativity Church in Evansville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Founded on September 16, 1997, it has 11 teachers and 53 students as of April 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Immediate access to many major forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation" title="Transportation">transportation</a> makes Evansville an important factor in Indiana's global economy. The city boasts road, rail, water, and air transportation systems. The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Regional_Airport" title="Evansville Regional Airport">Evansville Regional Airport</a>, housed in a 140,000-square-foot (13,000 m<sup>2</sup>) <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a>, offers nearly 30 flights a day to destinations around the country. Evansville does not have convenient access to commuter rail.</p>
<p>Evansville has a growing interstate system. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_64_(Indiana)" title="Interstate 64 (Indiana)">I-64</a> is eight miles north of the city and straddles the <a href="/wiki/Gibson_County,_Indiana" title="Gibson County, Indiana">Gibson</a> - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanderburgh_County" title="Vanderburgh County">Vanderburgh County</a> line. This interstate routes west to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> and runs east to <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_69_in_Indiana" title="Interstate 69 in Indiana">I-69</a> provides a convenient link from I-64 to the city's thriving eastside retail district and a direct route to the downtown business district via the <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Memorial_Parkway_(Evansville)" title="Veterans Memorial Parkway (Evansville)">Veterans Memorial Parkway</a>. It was also recently extended north to Indianapolis.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_41_(Indiana)" title="U.S. Highway 41 (Indiana)">U.S. Highway 41</a> connects the city with <a href="/wiki/Henderson,_Kentucky" title="Henderson, Kentucky">Henderson</a> to the south and, to the north, the cities of <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_Indiana" title="Princeton, Indiana">Princeton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincennes,_Indiana" title="Vincennes, Indiana">Vincennes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Terre_Haute,_Indiana" title="Terre Haute, Indiana">Terre Haute</a>. Other major local state roads include <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_Road_57" title="Indiana State Road 57">State Road 57</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_Road_62" title="Indiana State Road 62">State Road 62</a> (Morgan Avenue / <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Expressway" title="Lloyd Expressway">Lloyd Expressway</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_Road_66" title="Indiana State Road 66">State Road 66</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Expressway" title="Lloyd Expressway">Lloyd Expressway</a> / Diamond Avenue).</p>
<p>Public transit includes the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Evansville_Transit_System" title="Metropolitan Evansville Transit System">Metropolitan Evansville Transit System</a> (METS) which provides bus transportation to all sections of the city. Evansville has several multi-use trails for bikes and pedestrians, and in many areas there are on-road bike paths that help cyclists get around the city by bicycle. Like most cities, Evansville was served by electric <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcars" title="Streetcars">streetcars</a> into the 20th century.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evansville_Riverfront.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Evansville_Riverfront.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Evansville_Riverfront.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Evansville_Riverfront.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Evansville_Riverfront.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Evansville_Riverfront.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Evansville_Riverfront.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evansville_Riverfront.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Barges, like the one seen in the photo, can often be seen traveling up and down the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Evansville has historically been a major center for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway" title="Railway">railway</a> traffic. The <a href="/wiki/Evansville_and_Crawfordsville_Railroad" title="Evansville and Crawfordsville Railroad">Evansville and Crawfordsville Railroad</a> was first completed in 1853. Today, the city is served by four major freight railroads, <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX</a> (with a major yard in the Howell area), <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Western_Railway" title="Evansville Western Railway">Evansville Western Railway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Southwestern_Railway" title="Indiana Southwestern Railway">Indiana Southwestern Railway</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">Norfolk Southern Railway</a>. The Howell Yard in Evansville sorts and makes up trains, and has intermodal facilities to handle 3,000 cargo containers and piggyback trailers per month</p>
<p>Three public and several private port facilities receive year-round service from five major barge lines operating on the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>. The river connects Evansville with all river markets in the central <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and on the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> and with international markets through the port of <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>. Evansville has been a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Customs" title="United States Customs">U.S. Customs Port of Entry</a> for more than 125 years. Because of this, it is possible to have international cargo shipped to Evansville in bond. The international cargo can then clear Customs in Evansville rather than a coastal port.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">Electricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> are both provided to Evansville by <a href="/wiki/Vectren" title="Vectren">Vectren</a>. Water and sewer services are provided by the Evansville Water &amp; Sewer Company, which provides water to more than 75,000 customers in Evansville and the surrounding area. The <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> provides for most of the city's source of drinking water. Water is drawn from the river and filtered at a 60 million gallon per day treatment plant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> There are approximately 1,000 miles of water mains in the system and includes approximately 6,000 fire hydrants.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References_in_popular_culture">References in popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: References in popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Game scenes in the 1992 film <i><a href="/wiki/A_League_of_Their_Own" title="A League of Their Own">A League of Their Own</a></i> were filmed at <a href="/wiki/Bosse_Field" title="Bosse Field">Bosse Field</a>. It is the third oldest baseball stadium still in use in the United States (behind <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" title="Boston, Massachusetts">Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>). The ballpark served as the homefield for the <a href="/wiki/Racine_Belles" title="Racine Belles">Racine Belles</a>. Scenes from the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rosenbaum" title="Michael Rosenbaum">Michael Rosenbaum</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Back_in_the_Day_(2014_film)" title="Back in the Day (2014 film)">Back in the Day</a></i> feature Green River Road in Evansville.</p>
<p>All exterior shots on the 1988-1997 <a href="/wiki/Sitcom" title="Sitcom">sitcom</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roseanne_(TV_series)" title="Roseanne (TV series)">Roseanne</a></i> are still photographs taken in and around Evansville. The Connors' house is located at 619 South Runnymeade Avenue, and the Lobo Lounge is a pizzeria located at the corner of Edgar and Louisiana Streets. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matt_Williams_(producer)" title="Matt Williams (producer)">Matt Williams</a>, one of the show's producers, is a native of Evansville and a graduate of The University of Evansville theatre program. He is a co-founder of Wind Dancer Productions and has been involved with numerous sitcoms such as 'Home Improvement', movies and dramatic plays for Broadway.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i> has featured Evansville in two episodes. The first featured a story about comedian <a href="/wiki/Carrot_Top" title="Carrot Top">Carrot Top</a>'s reopening of the historic Victory Theatre. The second poked fun at former mayor Russel Lloyd Jr. for skipping out on a city meeting to attend <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>'s Farewell Tour concert being performed on the same night at Roberts Stadium.</p>
<p>Evansville was also featured in <a href="/wiki/Alton_Brown" title="Alton Brown">Alton Brown</a>'s series <i><a href="/wiki/Feasting_on_Asphalt" title="Feasting on Asphalt">Feasting on Asphalt</a></i>. Alton and his crew visited the historic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greyhound_Bus" title="Greyhound Bus">Greyhound Bus</a> station for its <a href="/wiki/Vending_machine" title="Vending machine">vending machines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/YWCA" title="YWCA">YWCA</a> tea room for lunch, and the <a class="external text" href="http://www.wegotbrains.com" rel="nofollow">Hilltop Inn</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Fried-brain_sandwich" title="Fried-brain sandwich">brain sandwich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burgoo" title="Burgoo">burgoo</a>. Other shows have included <i><a href="/wiki/Ghost_Hunters" title="Ghost Hunters">Ghost Hunters</a></i> which investigated <a href="/wiki/Willard_Library" title="Willard Library">Willard Library</a>'s "Gray Lady" ghost and <i><a href="/wiki/Storm_Stories" title="Storm Stories">Storm Stories</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/The_Weather_Channel" title="The Weather Channel">The Weather Channel</a> documenting the devastating <a href="/wiki/Evansville_Tornado_of_November_2005" title="Evansville Tornado of November 2005">tornado</a> that struck the city in 2005. The city was briefly featured in the 2007 <i><a href="/wiki/Prison_Break" title="Prison Break">Prison Break</a></i> episode "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago_(Prison_Break_episode)" title="Chicago (Prison Break episode)">Chicago</a>". In 2012, Evansville was featured on the British television program <a href="/wiki/Supersize_vs_Superskinny" title="Supersize vs Superskinny">Supersize vs Superskinny</a> because of a poll that ranked the residents of the city as the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obese" title="Obese">obese</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville and neighboring Newburgh was the featured location for the feature film "Back in the Day" filmed in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evansville is mentioned several times in the <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk_Empire_(season_3)" title="Boardwalk Empire (season 3)">third</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk_Empire_(season_4)" title="Boardwalk Empire (season 4)">fourth seasons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> series <a href="/wiki/Boardwalk_Empire" title="Boardwalk Empire">Boardwalk Empire</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_media">Literary media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Literary media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Evansville is featured in a section of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Nabokov" title="Vladimir Nabokov">Vladimir Nabokov</a>'s 1955 novel <a href="/wiki/Lolita" title="Lolita">Lolita</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Walker_Percy" title="Walker Percy">Walker Percy</a>'s 1962 novel <a href="/wiki/The_Moviegoer" title="The Moviegoer">The Moviegoer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Silverberg" title="Robert Silverberg">Robert Silverberg</a>'s 1969 science fiction novel <a href="/wiki/To_Live_Again_(novel)" title="To Live Again (novel)">To Live Again</a>.</p>
<p>Evansville is the primary location in the historical fiction novel, Invitation to Valhalla by Mike Whicker, published in 2004. The novel is based on the records of German spy <a href="/wiki/Erika_Lehmann" title="Erika Lehmann">Erika Lehmann</a>'s attempt to infiltrate the LST shipyards during WWII.</p>
<p>An Evansville couple is the focus of "Hungarian Rhapsody: An Adoption Story" by James Derk, based on a series of stories in The Evansville Courier &amp; Press<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Evansville,_Indiana" title="List of people from Evansville, Indiana">List of people from Evansville, Indiana</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Evansville,_Indiana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Evansville has three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_cities" title="Sister cities">sister cities</a>, as designated by <a href="/wiki/Sister_Cities_International" title="Sister Cities International">Sister Cities International</a>, Inc. (SCI):<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Osnabr%C3%BCck" title="Osnabrück">Osnabrück</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>, Germany</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico"><img alt="Mexico" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="840" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/46px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tizim%C3%ADn" title="Tizimín">Tizimín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucatán">Yucatán</a>, Mexico</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan"><img alt="Japan" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tochigi,_Tochigi" title="Tochigi, Tochigi">Tochigi-Shi</a>, Japan</li>
